<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maternal_changes">Maternal changes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bumm_123_lg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="955" data-file-width="1278" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bumm_123_lg.jpg/220px-Bumm_123_lg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bumm_123_lg.jpg/330px-Bumm_123_lg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Bumm_123_lg.jpg/440px-Bumm_123_lg.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bumm_123_lg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Uterus" title="Uterus">uterus</a> expands making up a larger and larger portion of the abdomen.  During the final stages of gestation the uterus may drop to a lower position.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maternal_physiological_changes_in_pregnancy" title="Maternal physiological changes in pregnancy">Maternal physiological changes in pregnancy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="978" decoding="async" height="77" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png/220px-Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png/330px-Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png/440px-Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breast_changes_during_pregnancy_1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Breast changes as seen during pregnancy. The areolae are larger and darker.</div></div></div>
<p>During pregnancy, a woman undergoes many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physiological" title="Physiological">physiological</a> changes, which are entirely normal, including <a href="/wiki/Parental_brain" title="Parental brain">behavioral</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiovascular" title="Cardiovascular">cardiovascular</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hematologic" title="Hematologic">hematologic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metabolic" title="Metabolic">metabolic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renal" title="Renal">renal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Respiration_(physiology)" title="Respiration (physiology)">respiratory</a> changes. Increases in <a href="/wiki/Blood_sugar_level" title="Blood sugar level">blood sugar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_rate" title="Respiratory rate">breathing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_output" title="Cardiac output">cardiac output</a> are all required. Levels of <a href="/wiki/Progesterone" title="Progesterone">progesterone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estrogen" title="Estrogen">estrogens</a> rise continually throughout pregnancy, suppressing the <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamic%E2%80%93pituitary%E2%80%93gonadal_axis" title="Hypothalamic–pituitary–gonadal axis">hypothalamic axis</a> and therefore also the <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_cycle" title="Menstrual cycle">menstrual cycle</a>. A full-term pregnancy at an early age (&lt; 25) reduces the risk of <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ovarian_cancer" title="Ovarian cancer">ovarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Endometrial_cancer" title="Endometrial cancer">endometrial cancer</a> and the risk declines further with each additional full-term pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1203" decoding="async" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg/170px-Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg/255px-Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg/340px-Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_26_weeks_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>End of second trimester + 2 weeks (26 weeks of pregnancy)</div></div></div>
<p>The fetus is <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetically</a> different from its mother, and can be viewed as an unusually successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allograft" title="Allograft">allograft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mor_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mor-51">[51]</a></sup> The main reason for this success is increased <a href="/wiki/Immune_tolerance_in_pregnancy" title="Immune tolerance in pregnancy">immune tolerance</a> during pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Immune tolerance is the concept that the body is able to not mount an immune system response against certain triggers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mor_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mor-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the first trimester, <a href="/wiki/Minute_ventilation" title="Minute ventilation">minute ventilation</a> increases by 40%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid11316633_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid11316633-53">[53]</a></sup> The womb will grow to the size of a lemon by eight weeks. Many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symptoms_and_discomforts_of_pregnancy" title="Symptoms and discomforts of pregnancy">symptoms and discomforts of pregnancy</a> like nausea and tender breasts appear in the first trimester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the second trimester, most women feel more energized, and begin to put on weight as the symptoms of morning sickness subside and eventually fade away. The uterus, the muscular organ that holds the developing fetus, can expand up to 20 times its normal size during pregnancy.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Braxton_Hicks_contractions" title="Braxton Hicks contractions">Braxton Hicks contractions</a> are sporadic uterine contractions that may start around six weeks into a pregnancy; however, they are usually not felt until the second or third trimester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hen2005_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hen2005-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Final weight gain takes place during the third trimester, which is the most weight gain throughout the pregnancy. The woman's abdomen will transform in shape as it drops due to the fetus turning in a downward position ready for birth. During the second trimester, the woman's abdomen would have been upright, whereas in the third trimester it will drop down low. The fetus moves regularly, and is felt by the woman. Fetal movement can become strong and be disruptive to the woman. The woman's <a href="/wiki/Navel" title="Navel">navel</a> will sometimes become convex, "popping" out, due to the expanding <a href="/wiki/Abdomen" title="Abdomen">abdomen</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1320" data-file-width="1632" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg/220px-Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg/330px-Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg/440px-Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Third_Trimester_pregnant_woman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Third trimester pregnant woman</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Head_engagement" title="Head engagement">Head engagement</a>, also called "lightening" or "dropping", occurs as the fetal head descends into a <a href="/wiki/Cephalic_presentation" title="Cephalic presentation">cephalic presentation</a>.  While it relieves pressure on the upper abdomen and gives a renewed ease in breathing, it also severely reduces bladder capacity resulting in a need to void more frequently, and increases pressure on the pelvic floor and the rectum.  It is not possible to predict when lightening occurs.  In a first pregnancy it may happen a few weeks before the due date, though it may happen later or even not until labor begins, as is typical with subsequent pregnancies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is also during the third trimester that maternal activity and sleep positions may affect fetal development due to restricted blood flow. For instance, the enlarged uterus may impede blood flow by compressing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vena_cava" title="Vena cava">vena cava</a> when lying flat, which is relieved by lying on the left side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21673002_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21673002-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childbirth">Childbirth</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">Childbirth</a></div>
<p>Childbirth, referred to as labor and delivery in the medical field, is the process whereby an infant is born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>A woman is considered to be in labour when she begins experiencing regular uterine contractions, accompanied by changes of her cervix—primarily effacement and dilation. While childbirth is widely experienced as painful, some women do report painless labours, while others find that concentrating on the birth helps to quicken labour and lessen the sensations. Most births are successful vaginal births, but sometimes complications arise and a woman may undergo a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cesarean_section" title="Cesarean section">cesarean section</a>.
</p><p>During the time immediately after birth, both the mother and the baby are hormonally cued to bond, the mother through the release of <a href="/wiki/Oxytocin" title="Oxytocin">oxytocin</a>, a hormone also released during <a href="/wiki/Breastfeeding" title="Breastfeeding">breastfeeding</a>. Studies show that skin-to-skin contact between a mother and her newborn immediately after birth is beneficial for both the mother and baby. A review done by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> found that skin-to-skin contact between mothers and babies after birth reduces crying, improves mother–infant interaction, and helps mothers to breastfeed successfully. They recommend that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neonates" title="Neonates">neonates</a> be allowed to bond with the mother during their first two hours after birth, the period that they tend to be more alert than in the following hours of early life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Childbirth_maturity_stages">Childbirth maturity stages</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">Preterm birth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Postterm_pregnancy" title="Postterm pregnancy">Postterm pregnancy</a></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Term"></span>
</p>
<table class="wikitable floatright">
<caption>Stages of pregnancy term
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>stage</th>
<th>starts</th>
<th>ends
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Preterm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preterm_definition_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-preterm_definition-60">[60]</a></sup></td>
<td style="text-align: center;">-</td>
<td>at 37 weeks
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Early term<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup></td>
<td>37 weeks</td>
<td>39 weeks
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Full term<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup></td>
<td>39 weeks</td>
<td>41 weeks
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Late term<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup></td>
<td>41 weeks</td>
<td>42 weeks
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Postterm<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup></td>
<td>42 weeks</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">-
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>In the ideal <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">childbirth</a> labor begins on its own when a woman is "at term".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACOGfive-2_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ACOGfive-2-17">[17]</a></sup>
Events before completion of 37 weeks are considered preterm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preterm_definition_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-preterm_definition-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">Preterm birth</a> is associated with a range of complications and should be avoided if possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SaigalDoyle2008_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-SaigalDoyle2008-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sometimes if a woman's <a href="/wiki/Rupture_of_membranes" title="Rupture of membranes">water breaks</a> or she has <a href="/wiki/Uterine_contraction" title="Uterine contraction">contractions</a> before 39 weeks, birth is unavoidable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-4"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup> However, spontaneous birth after 37 weeks is considered term and is not associated with the same risks of a preterm birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> Planned birth before 39 weeks by <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">caesarean section</a> or <a href="/wiki/Labor_induction" title="Labor induction">labor induction</a>, although "at term", results in an increased risk of complications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACOGfive-1_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACOGfive-1-63">[63]</a></sup> This is from factors including <a href="/wiki/Transient_tachypnea_of_the_newborn" title="Transient tachypnea of the newborn">underdeveloped lungs of newborns</a>, infection due to underdeveloped immune system, feeding problems due to underdeveloped brain, and <a href="/wiki/Jaundice" title="Jaundice">jaundice</a> from underdeveloped liver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr_July_2011_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-npr_July_2011-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Babies born between 39 and 41 weeks' gestation have better outcomes than babies born either before or after this range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-5"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup> This special time period is called "full term".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-6"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup> Whenever possible, waiting for labor to begin on its own in this time period is best for the health of the mother and baby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACOGfive-2_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-ACOGfive-2-17">[17]</a></sup> The decision to perform an induction must be made after weighing the risks and benefits, but is safer after 39 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACOGfive-2_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-ACOGfive-2-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Events after 42 weeks are considered <a href="/wiki/Postterm_pregnancy" title="Postterm pregnancy">postterm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-term_definition_61-7"><a href="#cite_note-term_definition-61">[61]</a></sup> When a pregnancy exceeds 42 weeks, the risk of complications for both the woman and the fetus increases significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UpToDate_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-UpToDate-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Therefore, in an otherwise uncomplicated pregnancy, obstetricians usually prefer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Induce_labour" title="Induce labour">induce labour</a> at some stage between 41 and 42 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postnatal_period">Postnatal period</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Postpartum_period" title="Postpartum period">Postpartum period</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Postpartum_period" title="Postpartum period">postpartum period</a> also referred to as the <i>puerperium</i>, is the postnatal period that begins immediately after delivery and extends for about six weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> During this period, the mother's body begins the return to pre-pregnancy conditions that includes changes in hormone levels and uterus size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</span></h2>
<p>The beginning of pregnancy may be detected either based on symptoms by the woman herself, or by using <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_test" title="Pregnancy test">pregnancy tests</a>. However, an important condition with serious health implications that is quite common is the <a href="/wiki/Denial_of_pregnancy" title="Denial of pregnancy">denial of pregnancy</a> by the pregnant woman. About 1 in 475 denials will last until around the 20th week of pregnancy. The proportion of cases of denial, persisting until delivery is about 1 in 2500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21725094_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21725094-68">[68]</a></sup> Conversely, some non-pregnant women have a very strong belief that they are pregnant along with some of the physical changes. This condition is known as a <a href="/wiki/False_pregnancy" title="False pregnancy">false pregnancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gabbe2012_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gabbe2012-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_signs">Physical signs</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Symptoms_and_discomforts_of_pregnancy" title="Symptoms and discomforts of pregnancy">Symptoms and discomforts of pregnancy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linea_nigra.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Linea_nigra.jpg/220px-Linea_nigra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Linea_nigra.jpg/330px-Linea_nigra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/Linea_nigra.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linea_nigra.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Linea_nigra" title="Linea nigra">Linea nigra</a> in a woman at 22 weeks pregnant</div></div></div>
<p>Most pregnant women experience a number of symptoms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pregnancy_symptoms_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-pregnancy_symptoms-70">[70]</a></sup> which can signify pregnancy. A number of early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_sign" title="Medical sign">medical signs</a> are associated with pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mayo_symptoms_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-mayo_symptoms-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Pregnancy_Association_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-American_Pregnancy_Association-72">[72]</a></sup> These signs include:
</p>
<ul><li>the presence of <a href="/wiki/Human_chorionic_gonadotropin" title="Human chorionic gonadotropin">human chorionic gonadotropin</a> (hCG) in the blood and urine</li>
<li>missed <a href="/wiki/Menstrual_cycle" title="Menstrual cycle">menstrual period</a></li>
<li>implantation bleeding that occurs at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Implantation_(human_embryo)" title="Implantation (human embryo)">implantation</a> of the embryo in the uterus during the third or fourth week after last menstrual period</li>
<li>increased <a href="/wiki/Basal_body_temperature" title="Basal body temperature">basal body temperature</a> sustained for over two weeks after <a href="/wiki/Ovulation" title="Ovulation">ovulation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chadwick%27s_sign" title="Chadwick's sign">Chadwick's sign</a> (darkening of the <a href="/wiki/Cervix" title="Cervix">cervix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vagina" title="Vagina">vagina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vulva" title="Vulva">vulva</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goodell%27s_sign" title="Goodell's sign">Goodell's sign</a> (softening of the vaginal portion of the cervix)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hegar%27s_sign" title="Hegar's sign">Hegar's sign</a> (softening of the <a href="/wiki/Uterine_isthmus" title="Uterine isthmus">uterine isthmus</a>)</li>
<li>Pigmentation of the <a href="/wiki/Linea_alba_(abdomen)" title="Linea alba (abdomen)">linea alba</a> – <a href="/wiki/Linea_nigra" title="Linea nigra">linea nigra</a>, (darkening of the skin in a midline of the <a href="/wiki/Abdomen" title="Abdomen">abdomen</a>, caused by <a href="/wiki/Hyperpigmentation" title="Hyperpigmentation">hyperpigmentation</a> resulting from hormonal changes, usually appearing around the middle of pregnancy).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mayo_symptoms_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-mayo_symptoms-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Pregnancy_Association_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-American_Pregnancy_Association-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li>Darkening of the nipples and areolas due to an increase in hormones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pregnancy_video_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-pregnancy_video-73">[73]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomarkers">Biomarkers</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_test" title="Pregnancy test">Pregnancy test</a></div>
<p>Pregnancy detection can be accomplished using one or more various <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_test" title="Pregnancy test">pregnancy tests</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pregnancy_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-pregnancy-74">[74]</a></sup> which detect hormones generated by the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Placenta" title="Placenta">placenta</a>, serving as <a href="/wiki/Biomarker_(medicine)" title="Biomarker (medicine)">biomarkers</a> of pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Blood and urine tests can detect pregnancy 12 days after implantation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Blood pregnancy tests are more sensitive than urine tests (giving fewer false negatives).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Home pregnancy tests are <a href="/wiki/Urine" title="Urine">urine</a> tests, and normally detect a pregnancy 12 to 15 days after fertilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-78">[78]</a></sup> A quantitative blood test can determine approximately the date the embryo was conceived because <a href="/wiki/Human_chorionic_gonadotropin" title="Human chorionic gonadotropin">hCG</a> doubles every 36 to 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-4"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> A single test of <a href="/wiki/Progesterone" title="Progesterone">progesterone</a> levels can also help determine how likely a fetus will survive in those with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Threatened_miscarriage" title="Threatened miscarriage">threatened miscarriage</a> (bleeding in early pregnancy).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid23045257_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23045257-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ultrasound">Ultrasound</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Obstetric_ultrasonography" title="Obstetric ultrasonography">Obstetric ultrasonography</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Obstetric_ultrasonography" title="Obstetric ultrasonography">Obstetric ultrasonography</a> can detect <a href="/wiki/List_of_fetal_abnormalities" title="List of fetal abnormalities">fetal abnormalities</a>, detect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_pregnancy" title="Multiple pregnancy">multiple pregnancies</a>, and improve gestational dating at 24 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The resultant estimated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestational_age_(obstetrics)" title="Gestational age (obstetrics)">gestational age</a> and due date of the fetus are slightly more accurate than methods based on last menstrual period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Ultrasound is used to measure the <a href="/wiki/Nuchal_scan" title="Nuchal scan">nuchal fold</a> in order to screen for <a href="/wiki/Down_syndrome" title="Down syndrome">Down syndrome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg"><img alt="An infographic showing a flow chart leading to three diagrams, each showing two human figures depicting different lengths of gestation, with a grid showing weight limits for different locations in front of the body" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1275" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg/250px-Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg/375px-Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg/500px-Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lifting_guidelines_during_pregnancy_-_NIOSH.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flowchart showing the recommended weight limits for lifting at work during pregnancy as a function of lifting frequency, weeks of gestation, and the position of the lifted object relative to the lifter's body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacDonaldWaters2013_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonaldWaters2013-84">[84]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prenatal_care">Prenatal care</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prenatal_care" title="Prenatal care">Prenatal care</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pre-conception_counseling" title="Pre-conception counseling">pre-conception counseling</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pre-conception_counseling" title="Pre-conception counseling">Pre-conception counseling</a> is care that is provided to a woman or couple to discuss conception, pregnancy, current health issues and recommendations for the period before pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prenatal_care" title="Prenatal care">Prenatal medical care</a> is the medical and nursing care recommended for women during pregnancy, time intervals and exact goals of each visit differ by country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Women who are high risk have better outcomes if they are seen regularly and frequently by a medical professional than women who are low risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> A woman can be labeled as high risk for different reasons including previous complications in pregnancy, complications in the current pregnancy, current medical diseases, or social issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>The aim of good prenatal care is prevention, early identification, and treatment of any medical complications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> A basic prenatal visit consists of measurement of blood pressure, <a href="/wiki/Fundal_height" title="Fundal height">fundal height</a>, weight and fetal heart rate, checking for symptoms of labor, and guidance for what to expect next.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyons_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition">Nutrition</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nutrition_and_pregnancy" title="Nutrition and pregnancy">Nutrition and pregnancy</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nutrition" title="Nutrition">Nutrition</a> during pregnancy is important to ensure healthy growth of the fetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-16">[16]</a></sup> Nutrition during pregnancy is different from the non-pregnant state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-16">[16]</a></sup> There are increased energy requirements and specific micronutrient requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-16">[16]</a></sup> Women benefit from education to encourage a balanced energy and protein intake during pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Some women may need professional medical advice if their diet is affected by medical conditions, food allergies, or specific religious/ ethical beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Further studies are needed to access the effect of dietary advice to prevent <a href="/wiki/Gestational_diabetes" title="Gestational diabetes">gestational diabetes</a>, although low quality evidence suggests some benefit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>Adequate periconceptional (time before and right after conception) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folic_acid" title="Folic acid">folic acid</a> (also called folate or Vitamin B<sub>9</sub>) intake has been shown to decrease the risk of fetal neural tube defects, such as <a href="/wiki/Spina_bifida" title="Spina bifida">spina bifida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16303691_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16303691-94">[94]</a></sup> The neural tube develops during the first 28 days of pregnancy, a urine pregnancy test is not usually positive until 14 days post-conception, explaining the necessity to guarantee adequate folate intake before conception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid11015508_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid11015508-95">[95]</a></sup> Folate is abundant in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_vegetables" title="Green vegetables">green leafy vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In the United States and Canada, most wheat products (flour, noodles) are fortified with folic acid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18185493_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid18185493-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weight_gain">Weight gain</span></h3>
<p>The amount of healthy weight gain during a pregnancy varies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRQ-weight_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-AHRQ-weight-98">[98]</a></sup> Weight gain is related to the weight of the baby, the placenta, extra circulatory fluid, larger tissues, and fat and protein stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-16">[16]</a></sup> Most needed weight gain occurs later in pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IQWiG-Weight_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-IQWiG-Weight-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a> recommends an overall pregnancy weight gain for those of normal weight (<a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">body mass index</a> of 18.5–24.9), of 11.3–15.9 kg (25–35 pounds) having a singleton pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Women who are underweight (BMI of less than 18.5), should gain between 12.7 and 18 kg (28–40 lb), while those who are <a href="/wiki/Overweight" title="Overweight">overweight</a> (BMI of 25–29.9) are advised to gain between 6.8 and 11.3 kg (15–25 lb) and those who are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obese" title="Obese">obese</a> (BMI ≥ 30) should gain between 5–9 kg (11–20 lb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid23262962_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid23262962-101">[101]</a></sup> These values reference the expectations for a term pregnancy.
</p><p>During pregnancy, insufficient or excessive weight gain can compromise the health of the mother and fetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IQWiG-Weight_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-IQWiG-Weight-99">[99]</a></sup> The most effective intervention for weight gain in underweight women is not clear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IQWiG-Weight_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-IQWiG-Weight-99">[99]</a></sup> Being or becoming overweight in pregnancy increases the risk of complications for mother and fetus, including <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">cesarean section</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gestational_hypertension" title="Gestational hypertension">gestational hypertension</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pre-eclampsia" title="Pre-eclampsia">pre-eclampsia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macrosomia" title="Macrosomia">macrosomia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shoulder_dystocia" title="Shoulder dystocia">shoulder dystocia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRQ-weight_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-AHRQ-weight-98">[98]</a></sup> Excessive weight gain can make losing weight after the pregnancy difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRQ-weight_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-AHRQ-weight-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHR-weight_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIHR-weight-102">[102]</a></sup> Some of these complications are risk factors for <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bushnell_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bushnell-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 50% of women of childbearing age in developed countries like the United Kingdom are overweight or obese before pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHR-weight_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIHR-weight-102">[102]</a></sup> Diet modification is the most effective way to reduce weight gain and associated risks in pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIHR-weight_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIHR-weight-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medication">Medication</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_drugs_in_pregnancy" title="Pharmaceutical drugs in pregnancy">Pharmaceutical drugs in pregnancy</a></div>
<p>Drugs used during pregnancy can have temporary or permanent effects on the fetus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Briggs_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Briggs-104">[104]</a></sup> Anything (including drugs) that can cause permanent deformities in the fetus are labeled as <a href="/wiki/Teratology" title="Teratology">teratogens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In the U.S., drugs were classified into categories A, B, C, D and X based on the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) rating system to provide therapeutic guidance based on potential benefits and fetal risks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Drugs, including some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multivitamins" title="Multivitamins">multivitamins</a>, that have demonstrated no fetal risks after controlled studies in humans are classified as Category A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Briggs_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Briggs-104">[104]</a></sup> On the other hand, drugs like <a href="/wiki/Thalidomide" title="Thalidomide">thalidomide</a> with proven fetal risks that outweigh all benefits are classified as Category X.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Briggs_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-Briggs-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational_drugs">Recreational drugs</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Neonatal_withdrawal" title="Neonatal withdrawal">Neonatal withdrawal</a></div>
<p>The use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recreational_drugs" title="Recreational drugs">recreational drugs</a> in pregnancy can cause various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pregnancy_complication" title="Pregnancy complication">pregnancy complications</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-5"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drinks" title="Alcoholic drinks">Alcoholic drinks</a> consumed during pregnancy can cause one or more <a href="/wiki/Fetal_alcohol_spectrum_disorder" title="Fetal alcohol spectrum disorder">fetal alcohol spectrum disorders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-6"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">CDC</a>, there is no known safe amount of alcohol during pregnancy and no safe time to drink during pregnancy, including before a woman knows that she is pregnant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking_and_pregnancy" title="Tobacco smoking and pregnancy">Tobacco smoking during pregnancy</a> can cause a wide range of behavioral, neurological, and physical difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackshaw_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hackshaw-108">[108]</a></sup> Smoking during pregnancy causes twice the risk of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premature_rupture_of_membranes" title="Premature rupture of membranes">premature rupture of membranes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Placental_abruption" title="Placental abruption">placental abruption</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Placenta_previa" title="Placenta previa">placenta previa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_preventing_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_preventing-109">[109]</a></sup> Smoking is associated with 30% higher odds of preterm birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC_tobacco_use_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC_tobacco_use-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prenatal_cocaine_exposure" title="Prenatal cocaine exposure">Prenatal cocaine exposure</a> is associated with <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">premature birth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birth_defect" title="Birth defect">birth defects</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attention_deficit_disorder" title="Attention deficit disorder">attention deficit disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-7"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine#Methamphetamine_babies" title="Methamphetamine">Prenatal methamphetamine exposure</a> can cause premature birth and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congenital_abnormalities" title="Congenital abnormalities">congenital abnormalities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fact_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fact-111">[111]</a></sup> Short-term neonatal outcomes in <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine#Methamphetamine_babies" title="Methamphetamine">methamphetamine babies</a> show small deficits in infant neurobehavioral function and growth restriction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grotta_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grotta-112">[112]</a></sup> Long-term effects in terms of impaired brain development may also be caused by <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine" title="Methamphetamine">methamphetamine</a> use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fact_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fact-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cannabis_in_pregnancy" title="Cannabis in pregnancy">Cannabis in pregnancy</a> has been shown to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teratogenic" title="Teratogenic">teratogenic</a> in large doses in animals, but has not shown any teratogenic effects in humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-8"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exposure_to_toxins">Exposure to toxins<span class="anchor" id="Environmental_toxicants_and_fetal_development"></span><span class="anchor" id="Exposure_to_environmental_toxins"></span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_toxicants_and_fetal_development" title="Environmental toxicants and fetal development">Environmental toxicants and fetal development</a></div>
