<p>Intrauterine exposure to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_toxins_in_pregnancy" title="Environmental toxins in pregnancy">environmental toxins in pregnancy</a> has the potential to cause adverse effects on <a href="/wiki/Prenatal_development" title="Prenatal development">prenatal development</a>, and to cause <a href="/wiki/Complications_of_pregnancy" title="Complications of pregnancy">pregnancy complications</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-9"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> Air pollution has been associated with low birth weight infants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Conditions of particular severity in pregnancy include <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lead_poisoning" title="Lead poisoning">lead poisoning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_58-10"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-58">[58]</a></sup> To minimize exposure to environmental toxins, the American College of Nurse-Midwives recommends: checking whether the home has <a href="/wiki/Lead_paint" title="Lead paint">lead paint</a>, washing all fresh <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a> thoroughly and buying <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">organic</a> produce, and avoiding cleaning products labeled "toxic" or any product with a warning on the label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pregnant women can also be exposed to <a href="/wiki/Chemical_hazard" title="Chemical hazard">toxins in the workplace</a>, including airborne particles. The effects of wearing N95 filtering facepiece <a href="/wiki/Respirator" title="Respirator">respirators</a> are similar for pregnant women as for non-pregnant women, and wearing a respirator for one hour does not affect the fetal heart rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_activity">Sexual activity</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_activity_during_pregnancy" title="Sexual activity during pregnancy">Sexual activity during pregnancy</a></div>
<p>Most women can continue to engage in sexual activity, including <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a>, throughout pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prenatal_Care_chapter_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prenatal_Care_chapter-116">[116]</a></sup> Most research suggests that during pregnancy both sexual desire and frequency of sexual relations decrease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bermudez_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bermudez-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fok_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fok-118">[118]</a></sup> In context of this overall decrease in desire, some studies indicate a second-trimester increase, preceding a decrease during the third trimester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reamy_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reamy-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sex during pregnancy is a low-risk behavior except when the healthcare provider advises that sexual intercourse be avoided for particular medical reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prenatal_Care_chapter_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prenatal_Care_chapter-116">[116]</a></sup> For a healthy pregnant woman, there is no single <i>safe</i> or <i>right</i> way to have sex during pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prenatal_Care_chapter_116-2"><a href="#cite_note-Prenatal_Care_chapter-116">[116]</a></sup> Pregnancy alters the <a href="/wiki/List_of_microbiota_species_of_the_lower_reproductive_tract_of_women" title="List of microbiota species of the lower reproductive tract of women">vaginal flora</a> with a reduction in microscopic species/genus diversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClarkTal2014_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClarkTal2014-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exercise">Exercise</span></h3>
<p>Regular <a href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercise" title="Aerobic exercise">aerobic exercise</a> during pregnancy appears to improve (or maintain) physical fitness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_exercise" title="Physical exercise">Physical exercise</a> during pregnancy appears to decrease the need for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-section" title="C-section">C-section</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and even vigorous exercise carries no significant risks to babies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetham2019_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beetham2019-124">[124]</a></sup> and provides significant health benefits to the mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DiMascio2016_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-DiMascio2016-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bed_rest" title="Bed rest">Bed rest</a>, outside of research studies, is not recommended as there is no evidence of benefit and potential harm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Clinical Practice Obstetrics Committee of Canada recommends that "All women without contraindications should be encouraged to participate in aerobic and strength-conditioning exercises as part of a healthy lifestyle during their pregnancy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-127">[127]</a></sup> Although an upper level of safe exercise intensity has not been established, women who were regular exercisers before pregnancy and who have uncomplicated pregnancies should be able to engage in high intensity exercise programs, without a higher risk of prematurity, lower birth weight, or gestational weight gain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beetham2019_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beetham2019-124">[124]</a></sup> In general, participation in a wide range of recreational activities appears to be safe, with the avoidance of those with a high risk of falling such as horseback riding or skiing or those that carry a risk of abdominal trauma, such as soccer or hockey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12547738_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid12547738-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>The American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists reports that in the past, the main concerns of exercise in pregnancy were focused on the fetus and any potential maternal benefit was thought to be offset by potential risks to the fetus. However, they write that more recent information suggests that in the uncomplicated pregnancy, fetal injuries are highly unlikely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12547738_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid12547738-128">[128]</a></sup> They do, however, list several circumstances when a woman should contact her healthcare provider before continuing with an exercise program: vaginal bleeding, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dyspnea" title="Dyspnea">dyspnea</a> before exertion, dizziness, headache, chest pain, muscle weakness, preterm labor, decreased fetal movement, amniotic fluid leakage, and calf pain or swelling (to rule out <a href="/wiki/Thrombophlebitis" title="Thrombophlebitis">thrombophlebitis</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12547738_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-pmid12547738-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep">Sleep</span></h3>
<p>It has been suggested that <a href="/wiki/Shift_work" title="Shift work">shift work</a> and exposure to bright light at night should be avoided at least during the last trimester of pregnancy to decrease the risk of psychological and behavioral problems in the newborn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReiterTan2013_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReiterTan2013-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dental_care">Dental care</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prenatal_dental_care" title="Prenatal dental care">Prenatal dental care</a></div>
<p>The increased levels of <a href="/wiki/Progesterone" title="Progesterone">progesterone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estrogen" title="Estrogen">estrogen</a> during pregnancy make <a href="/wiki/Gingivitis" title="Gingivitis">gingivitis</a> more likely; the <a href="/wiki/Gums" title="Gums">gums</a> become edematous, red in colour, and tend to bleed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Also a <a href="/wiki/Pyogenic_granuloma" title="Pyogenic granuloma">pyogenic granuloma</a> or "pregnancy tumor", is commonly seen on the labial surface of the papilla. Lesions can be treated by local debridement or deep incision depending on their size, and by following adequate <a href="/wiki/Oral_hygiene" title="Oral hygiene">oral hygiene</a> measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> There have been suggestions that severe <a href="/wiki/Periodontal_disease" title="Periodontal disease">periodontitis</a> may increase the risk of having <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">preterm birth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Low_birth_weight" title="Low birth weight">low birth weight</a>; however, a Cochrane review found insufficient evidence to determine if <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Periodontitis" title="Periodontitis">periodontitis</a> can develop adverse birth outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid28605006_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid28605006-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flying">Flying</span></h3>
<p>In low risk pregnancies, most health care providers approve flying until about 36 weeks of gestational age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Most airlines allow pregnant women to fly short distances at less than 36 weeks, and long distances at less than 32 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jarvis_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-134">[134]</a></sup> Many airlines require a doctor's note that approves flying, especially at over 28 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jarvis_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-134">[134]</a></sup> During flights, the risk of <a href="/wiki/Deep_vein_thrombosis" title="Deep vein thrombosis">deep vein thrombosis</a> is decreased by getting up and walking occasionally, as well as by avoiding dehydration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jarvis_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Full_body_scanner" title="Full body scanner">Full body scanners</a> do not use ionizing radiation, and are safe in pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Airports can also possibly use <a href="/wiki/Full_body_scanner#Backscatter_X-ray_scanners" title="Full body scanner">backscatter X-ray scanners</a>, which use a very low dose, but where safety in pregnancy is not fully established.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Complications">Complications</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Complications_of_pregnancy" title="Complications of pregnancy">Complications of pregnancy</a></div>
<p>Each year, ill health as a result of pregnancy is experienced (sometimes permanently) by more than 20 million women around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Reproductive_Health_and_Research_Publications:_Making_Pregnancy_Safer_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_Reproductive_Health_and_Research_Publications:_Making_Pregnancy_Safer-136">[136]</a></sup> In 2016, complications of pregnancy resulted in 230,600 deaths down from 377,000 deaths in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GBD2016_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-GBD2016-12">[12]</a></sup> Common causes include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_bleeding" title="Maternal bleeding">bleeding</a> (72,000), <a href="/wiki/Postpartum_infections" title="Postpartum infections">infections</a> (20,000), <a href="/wiki/Hypertensive_disease_of_pregnancy" title="Hypertensive disease of pregnancy">hypertensive diseases of pregnancy</a> (32,000), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obstructed_labor" title="Obstructed labor">obstructed labor</a> (10,000), and <a href="/wiki/Category:Pregnancy_with_abortive_outcome" title="Category:Pregnancy with abortive outcome">pregnancy with abortive outcome</a> (20,000), which includes <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ectopic_pregnancy" title="Ectopic pregnancy">ectopic pregnancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GBD2016_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-GBD2016-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The following are some examples of pregnancy complications:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pregnancy_induced_hypertension" title="Pregnancy induced hypertension">Pregnancy induced hypertension</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">Anemia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Postpartum_depression" title="Postpartum depression">Postpartum depression</a>, a common but solvable complication following childbirth that may result from decreased hormonal levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Postpartum_psychosis" title="Postpartum psychosis">Postpartum psychosis</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Venous_thrombosis" title="Venous thrombosis">Thromboembolic disorders</a>, with an increased risk due to <a href="/wiki/Hypercoagulability_in_pregnancy" title="Hypercoagulability in pregnancy">hypercoagulability in pregnancy</a>. These are the leading cause of death in pregnant women in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lev2013_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lev2013-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pruritic_urticarial_papules_and_plaques_of_pregnancy" title="Pruritic urticarial papules and plaques of pregnancy">Pruritic urticarial papules and plaques of pregnancy</a> (PUPPP), a skin disease that develops around the 32nd week. Signs are red plaques, papules, and itchiness around the belly button that then spreads all over the body except for the inside of hands and face.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ectopic_pregnancy" title="Ectopic pregnancy">Ectopic pregnancy</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Abdominal_pregnancy" title="Abdominal pregnancy">abdominal pregnancy</a>, implantation of the embryo outside the uterus</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hyperemesis_gravidarum" title="Hyperemesis gravidarum">Hyperemesis gravidarum</a>, excessive nausea and vomiting that is more severe than normal morning sickness.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_embolism" title="Pulmonary embolism">Pulmonary embolism</a>, a blood clot that forms in the legs and migrates to the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lev2013_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lev2013-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Acute_fatty_liver_of_pregnancy" title="Acute fatty liver of pregnancy">Acute fatty liver of pregnancy</a> is a rare complication thought to be brought about by a disruption in the metabolism of fatty acids by <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">mitochondria</a>.</li></ul>
<p>There is also an increased <a href="/wiki/Susceptibility_and_severity_of_infections_in_pregnancy" title="Susceptibility and severity of infections in pregnancy">susceptibility and severity of certain infections in pregnancy</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscarriage_and_stillbirth">Miscarriage and stillbirth</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">Miscarriage</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">Stillbirth</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage_and_grief" title="Miscarriage and grief">Miscarriage and grief</a></div>
<p>Miscarriage is the most common complication of early pregnancy.  It is defined as the loss of an embryo or fetus before it is able to survive independently.  The most common symptom of miscarriage is vaginal bleeding with or without pain. The miscarriage may be evidenced by a clot-like material passing through and out of the vagina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>  About 80% of miscarriages occur in the first 12 weeks of pregnancy. The underlying cause in about half of cases involves chromosomal abnormalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Stillbirth is defined as fetal death after 20 or 28 weeks of pregnancy, depending on the source. It results in a baby born without signs of life.  Each year about 21,000 babies are stillborn in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Sadness, anxiety, and guilt may occur after a miscarriage or a stillbirth.  Emotional support may help with processing the loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>Fathers may experience grief over the loss as well.  A large study found that there is a need to increase the accessibility of support services available for fathers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diseases_in_pregnancy">Diseases in pregnancy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Pre-existing_disease_in_pregnancy" title="Pre-existing disease in pregnancy">Pre-existing disease in pregnancy</a></div>
<p>A pregnant woman may have a <a href="/wiki/Pre-existing_disease_in_pregnancy" title="Pre-existing disease in pregnancy">pre-existing disease</a>, which is not directly caused by the pregnancy, but may cause <a href="/wiki/Complications_of_pregnancy" title="Complications of pregnancy">complications</a> to develop that include a potential risk to the pregnancy; or a disease may develop during pregnancy.
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_and_pregnancy" title="Diabetes mellitus and pregnancy">Diabetes mellitus and pregnancy</a> deals with the interactions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes mellitus</a> (not restricted to <a href="/wiki/Gestational_diabetes" title="Gestational diabetes">gestational diabetes</a>) and pregnancy. Risks for the child include miscarriage, growth restriction, growth acceleration, <a href="/wiki/Large_for_gestational_age" title="Large for gestational age">large for gestational age</a> (macrosomia), <a href="/wiki/Polyhydramnios" title="Polyhydramnios">polyhydramnios</a> (too much <a href="/wiki/Amniotic_fluid" title="Amniotic fluid">amniotic fluid</a>), and birth defects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thyroid_disease_in_pregnancy" title="Thyroid disease in pregnancy">Thyroid disease in pregnancy</a> can, if uncorrected, cause adverse effects on fetal and maternal well-being. The deleterious effects of thyroid dysfunction can also extend beyond pregnancy and delivery to affect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developmental_milestone" title="Developmental milestone">neurointellectual development</a> in the early life of the child. Demand for thyroid hormones is increased during pregnancy, which may cause a previously unnoticed thyroid disorder to worsen.</li>
<li>Untreated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celiac_disease" title="Celiac disease">celiac disease</a> can cause a <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intrauterine_growth_restriction" title="Intrauterine growth restriction">intrauterine growth restriction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Small_for_gestational_age" title="Small for gestational age">small for gestational age</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_birthweight" title="Low birthweight">low birthweight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">preterm birth</a>. Often <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_system_disease" title="Reproductive system disease">reproductive disorders</a> are the only manifestation of undiagnosed celiac disease and most cases are not recognized. Complications or failures of pregnancy cannot be explained simply by <a href="/wiki/Malabsorption" title="Malabsorption">malabsorption</a>, but by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autoimmmune_response" title="Autoimmmune response">autoimmune response</a> elicited by the exposure to <a href="/wiki/Gluten" title="Gluten">gluten</a>, which causes damage to the <a href="/wiki/Placenta" title="Placenta">placenta</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gluten-free_diet" title="Gluten-free diet">gluten-free diet</a> avoids or reduces the risk of developing reproductive disorders in pregnant women with celiac disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TersigniCastellani2014_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-TersigniCastellani2014-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SacconeBerghella2015_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-SacconeBerghella2015-147">[147]</a></sup> Also, pregnancy can be a trigger for the development of celiac disease in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_susceptibility" title="Genetic susceptibility">genetically susceptible</a> women who are consuming gluten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glutengovca_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glutengovca-148">[148]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lupus_and_pregnancy" title="Lupus and pregnancy">Lupus in pregnancy</a> confers an increased rate of fetal death <i>in utero,</i> miscarriage, and of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neonatal_lupus" title="Neonatal lupus">neonatal lupus</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hypercoagulability_in_pregnancy" title="Hypercoagulability in pregnancy">Hypercoagulability in pregnancy</a> is the propensity of pregnant women to develop <a href="/wiki/Thrombosis" title="Thrombosis">thrombosis</a> (blood clots). Pregnancy itself is a factor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypercoagulability" title="Hypercoagulability">hypercoagulability</a> (pregnancy-induced hypercoagulability), as a physiologically adaptive mechanism to prevent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postpartum_hemorrhage" title="Postpartum hemorrhage">postpartum bleeding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gresele_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-gresele-149">[149]</a></sup> However, in combination with an underlying hypercoagulable state, the risk of thrombosis or embolism may become substantial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gresele_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-gresele-149">[149]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion">Abortion</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">Abortion</a></div>
<p>An abortion is the termination of an embryo or fetus, either naturally (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spontaneous_abortion" title="Spontaneous abortion">spontaneous abortion</a>) or via medical methods (<a href="/wiki/Abortion#Induced" title="Abortion">induced abortion</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>When carried out by choice, it is usually within the first trimester, sometimes in the second, and rarely in the third.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sharply_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-sharply-45">[45]</a></sup> Reasons for <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">pregnancies being undesired</a> are broad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zdanowicz_2019_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zdanowicz_2019-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> being the most legally accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Center_for_Reproductive_Rights_2022_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Center_for_Reproductive_Rights_2022-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_control_and_education">Birth control and education</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">Birth control</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">Family planning</a>, as well as the availability and use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraception" title="Contraception">contraception</a>, along with increased <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_sex_education" title="Comprehensive sex education">comprehensive sex education</a>, has enabled many to prevent pregnancies when they are not desired. Schemes and funding to support education and the means to prevent pregnancies when they are not intended have been instrumental and are part of the third of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> (SDGs) advanced by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_Division_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Population_Division-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technologies_and_science">Technologies and science</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Obstetrics" title="Obstetrics">Obstetrics</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assisted_reproductive_technology">Assisted reproductive technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Assisted_reproductive_technology" title="Assisted reproductive technology">Assisted reproductive technology</a></div>
<p>Modern reproductive medicine offers many forms of assisted reproductive technology for couples who stay childless against their will, such as <a href="/wiki/Fertility_medication" title="Fertility medication">fertility medication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination" title="Artificial insemination">artificial insemination</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilization" title="In vitro fertilization"><i>in vitro</i> fertilization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surrogacy" title="Surrogacy">surrogacy</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_imaging">Medical imaging</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_(smaller).gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="708" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif/220px-Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif/330px-Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif/440px-Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_%28smaller%29.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volume_rendered_CT_scan_of_a_pregnancy_of_37_weeks_of_gestational_age_(smaller).gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CT_scan" title="CT scan">CT scanning</a> (<a href="/wiki/Volume_rendering" title="Volume rendering">volume rendered</a> in this case) confers a <a href="/wiki/Absorbed_dose" title="Absorbed dose">radiation dose</a> to the developing fetus.</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg/220px-Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg/330px-Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg/440px-Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pregnancy_Check_Up.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pregnant woman undergoing an <a href="/wiki/Ultrasound" title="Ultrasound">ultrasound</a>. Ultrasound is used to check on the growth and development of the fetus.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging_in_pregnancy" title="Medical imaging in pregnancy">Medical imaging in pregnancy</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">Medical imaging</a> may be <a href="/wiki/Indication_(medicine)" title="Indication (medicine)">indicated</a> in pregnancy because of <a href="/wiki/Complications_of_pregnancy" title="Complications of pregnancy">pregnancy complications</a>, disease, or routine <a href="/wiki/Prenatal_care" title="Prenatal care">prenatal care</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_ultrasonography" title="Medical ultrasonography">Medical ultrasonography</a> including <a href="/wiki/Obstetric_ultrasonography" title="Obstetric ultrasonography">obstetric ultrasonography</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging_in_pregnancy" title="Magnetic resonance imaging in pregnancy">magnetic resonance imaging (MRI)</a> without <a href="/wiki/MRI_contrast_agent" title="MRI contrast agent">contrast agents</a> are not associated with any risk for the mother or the fetus, and are the imaging techniques of choice for pregnant women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acog_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-acog-154">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Projectional_radiography" title="Projectional radiography">Projectional radiography</a>, <a href="/wiki/CT_scan" title="CT scan">CT scan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_medicine#Diagnostic" title="Nuclear medicine">nuclear medicine imaging</a> result in some degree of <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">ionizing radiation</a> exposure, but in most cases the <a href="/wiki/Absorbed_dose" title="Absorbed dose">absorbed doses</a> are not associated with harm to the baby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acog_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-acog-154">[154]</a></sup> At higher dosages, effects can include <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birth_defect" title="Birth defect">birth defects</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_disability" title="Intellectual disability">intellectual disability</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acog_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-acog-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_rate" title="Pregnancy rate">Pregnancy rate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Advanced_maternal_age" title="Advanced maternal age">Advanced maternal age</a></div>
<p>About 213 million pregnancies occurred in 2012 of which 190 million were in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">developing world</a> and 23 million were in the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sed2014_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sed2014-11">[11]</a></sup> This is about 133 pregnancies per 1,000 women aged 15 to 44.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sed2014_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sed2014-11">[11]</a></sup> About 10% to 15% of recognized pregnancies end in miscarriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-John2012_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-John2012-2">[2]</a></sup> Globally, 44% of pregnancies are <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">unplanned</a>. Over half (56%) of unplanned pregnancies are aborted. In countries where <a href="/wiki/Abortion_law" title="Abortion law">abortion is prohibited</a>, or only carried out in circumstances where the mother's life is at risk, 48% of unplanned pregnancies are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_abortion" title="Illegal abortion">aborted illegally</a>. Compared to the rate in countries where abortion is legal, at 69%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bea2018_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bea2018-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>Of pregnancies in 2012, 120 million occurred in Asia, 54 million in Africa, 19 million in Europe, 18 million in Latin America and the Caribbean, 7 million in North America, and 1 million in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sed2014_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sed2014-11">[11]</a></sup> Pregnancy rates are 140 per 1000 women of childbearing age in the developing world and 94 per 1000 in the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sed2014_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-Sed2014-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The rate of pregnancy, as well as the ages at which it occurs, differ by country and region. It is influenced by a number of factors, such as cultural, social and religious norms; access to contraception; and rates of education. The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) in 2013 was estimated to be highest in <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> (7.03 children/woman) and lowest in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (0.79 children/woman).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Europe, the average childbearing age has been rising continuously for some time. In Western, Northern, and Southern Europe, first-time mothers are on average 26 to 29 years old, up from 23 to 25 years at the start of the 1970s. In a number of European countries (Spain), the mean age of women at first childbirth has crossed the 30-year threshold.
</p><p>This process is not restricted to Europe. Asia, Japan and the United States are all seeing average age at first birth on the rise, and increasingly the process is spreading to countries in the developing world like China, Turkey and Iran. In the US, the average age of first childbirth was 25.4 in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States and United Kingdom, 40% of pregnancies are <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">unplanned</a>, and between a quarter and half of those unplanned pregnancies were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unwanted_pregnancies" title="Unwanted pregnancies">unwanted pregnancies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the US, a woman's educational attainment and her marital status are correlated with childbearing: the percentage of women unmarried at the time of first birth drops with increasing educational level. In other words: among uneducated women, a large fraction (~80%) have their first child while they are unmarried. By contrast, few women with a bachelor's degree or higher (~25%) have their first child while unmarried. However, this phenomenon also has a strong generational component: in 1996, about 50% of women without a university degree had their first child being unmarried while that number increased to ~85% in 2018. Similarly, in 1996, only 4% of women with a BA degree or similar had their first child being unmarried. In 2018, that fraction increased to ~25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_and_social_aspects">Legal and social aspects</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_and_reproductive_health" title="Sexual and reproductive health">Sexual and reproductive health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy" title="Teenage pregnancy">Teenage pregnancy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_over_age_50" title="Pregnancy over age 50">Pregnancy over age 50</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_protection">Legal protection</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">Reproductive rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_justice" title="Reproductive justice">Reproductive justice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Female_reproductive_system" title="Female reproductive system">Female reproductive system</a></div>
<p>Many countries have various legal regulations in place to protect pregnant women and their children. Many countries have laws against <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_discrimination" title="Pregnancy discrimination">pregnancy discrimination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maternity_Protection_Convention,_2000" title="Maternity Protection Convention, 2000">Maternity Protection Convention</a> ensures that pregnant women are exempt from activities such as night shifts or carrying heavy stocks. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternity_leave" title="Maternity leave">Maternity leave</a> typically provides paid leave from work during roughly the last trimester of pregnancy and for some time after birth. Notable extreme cases include Norway (8 months with full pay) and the United States (no paid leave at all except in some states). 
</p><p>In the United States, some actions that result in miscarriage or stillbirth, such as beating a pregnant woman, are considered crimes. One law that does so is the federal <a href="/wiki/Unborn_Victims_of_Violence_Act" title="Unborn Victims of Violence Act">Unborn Victims of Violence Act</a>. In 2014, the American state of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> passed a law which allows prosecutors to charge a woman with criminal assault if she uses illegal drugs during her pregnancy and her fetus or newborn is harmed as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, protections are not universal.  In <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, the <i>Employment of Foreign Manpower Act</i> forbids current and former <a href="/wiki/Work_permit" title="Work permit">work permit</a> holders from becoming pregnant or giving birth in Singapore without prior permission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yale_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-yale-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Violation of the Act is punishable by a fine of up to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_dollar" title="Singapore dollar">S$</a>10,000 (US$7300) and <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yale_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-yale-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> and until 2010, their employers would lose their $5,000 security bond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racial_disparities">Racial disparities</span></h3>
<p>There are significant racial imbalances in pregnancy and neonatal care systems. Midwifery guidance, treatment, and care have been related to better birth outcomes. Diminishing racial inequities in health is an increasingly large public health challenge in the United States. Despite the fact that average rates have decreased, data on neonatal mortality demonstrates that racial disparities have persisted and grown. The death rate for African American babies is nearly double that of white neonates. According to studies, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birth_defects" title="Birth defects">congenital defects</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudden_infant_death_syndrome" title="Sudden infant death syndrome">SIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">preterm birth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Low_birth_weight" title="Low birth weight">low birth weight</a> are all more common among African American babies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guerra-Reyes_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guerra-Reyes-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Midwifery care has been linked to better birth and postpartum outcomes for both mother and child. It caters to the needs of the woman and provides competent, sympathetic care, and is essential for maternal health improvement. The presence of a doula, or birth assistant, during labor and delivery, has also been associated with improved levels of satisfaction with medical birth care. Providers recognized their profession from a historical standpoint, a link to African origins, the diaspora, and prevailing African American struggles. Providers participated in both direct clinical experience and activist involvement. Advocacy efforts aimed to enhance the number of minority birth attendants and to promote the benefits of woman-centered birth care to neglected areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guerra-Reyes_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guerra-Reyes-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transgender_people">Transgender  people</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transgender_pregnancy" title="Transgender pregnancy">Transgender pregnancy</a></div>
<p>Regardless of prior hormone replacement therapy treatments, the progression of pregnancy and birthing procedures for <a href="/wiki/Transgender_pregnancy" title="Transgender pregnancy">transgender people who carry pregnancies</a>  are typically the same as those of <a href="/wiki/Cisgender" title="Cisgender">cisgender</a> women.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, they may be subjected to discrimination, which can include a variety of negative social, emotional, and medical experiences, as pregnancy is regarded as an exclusively female activity. According to a study by the <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Obstetricians_and_Gynecologists" title="American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists">American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists</a>, there is a lack of awareness, services, and medical assistance available to pregnant trans men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG/220px-Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG/330px-Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG/440px-Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Church_of_the_Visitation_IMG_0637.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Visitation_(Christianity)" title="Visitation (Christianity)">The Visitation</a>: <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary</a>, pregnant with <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, visiting pregnant <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_(biblical_figure)" title="Elizabeth (biblical figure)">Elizabeth</a>, depicted as a statue at the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Visitation" title="Church of the Visitation">Church of the Visitation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ein_Karem" title="Ein Karem">Ein Karem</a>, Israel.</div></div></div>
<p>In most cultures, pregnant women have a special status in society and receive particularly gentle care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isbn_9780759110441_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-isbn_9780759110441-168">[168]</a></sup> At the same time, they are subject to expectations that may exert great psychological pressure, such as having to produce a son and heir. In many traditional societies, pregnancy must be preceded by marriage, on pain of ostracism of mother and <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(family_law)" title="Legitimacy (family law)">(illegitimate) child</a>.
</p><p>Overall, pregnancy is accompanied by numerous customs that are often subject to ethnological research, often rooted in <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional medicine</a> or religion. The <a href="/wiki/Baby_shower" title="Baby shower">baby shower</a> is an example of a modern custom.
</p><p>Pregnancy is an important topic in <a href="/wiki/Sociology_of_the_family" title="Sociology of the family">sociology of the family</a>. The prospective child may preliminarily be placed into numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_role" title="Social role">social roles</a>. The parents' relationship and the relation between parents and their surroundings are also affected.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Belly_cast" title="Belly cast">belly cast</a> may be made during pregnancy as a keepsake.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_in_art" title="Pregnancy in art">Pregnancy in art</a></div>
<p>Images of pregnant women, especially small <a href="/wiki/Figurine" title="Figurine">figurines</a>, were made in traditional cultures in many places and periods, though it is rarely one of the most common types of image. These include ceramic figures from some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</a> cultures, and a few figures from most of the ancient Mediterranean cultures. Many of these seem to be connected with <a href="/wiki/Fertility_in_art" title="Fertility in art">fertility</a>. Identifying whether such figures are actually meant to show pregnancy is often a problem, as well as understanding their role in the culture concerned.
</p><p>Among the oldest surviving examples of the depiction of pregnancy are prehistoric figurines found across much of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> and collectively known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venus_figurines" title="Venus figurines">Venus figurines</a>. Some of these appear to be pregnant.
</p><p>Due to the important role of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_of_God" title="Mother of God">Mother of God</a> in <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, the Western visual arts have a long tradition of depictions of pregnancy, especially in the biblical scene of the <a href="/wiki/Visitation_(Christianity)" title="Visitation (Christianity)">Visitation</a>, and devotional images called a <i><a href="/wiki/Madonna_del_Parto" title="Madonna del Parto">Madonna del Parto</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>The unhappy scene usually called <i>Diana and Callisto</i>, showing the moment of discovery of <a href="/wiki/Callisto_(mythology)" title="Callisto (mythology)">Callisto</a>'s forbidden pregnancy, is sometimes painted from the Renaissance onwards. Gradually, portraits of pregnant women began to appear, with a particular fashion for "pregnancy portraits" in elite portraiture of the years around 1600.
</p><p>Pregnancy, and especially pregnancy of unmarried women, is also an important motif in literature. Notable examples include <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a>'s 1891 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Tess_of_the_d%27Urbervilles" title="Tess of the d'Urbervilles">Tess of the d'Urbervilles</a></i> and Goethe's 1808 play <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faust:_The_First_Part_of_the_Tragedy" title="Faust: The First Part of the Tragedy">Faust</a></i>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Tay2011-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Tay2011_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Tay2011_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span
